Donald Trump issues order to ban Tik TokCE Noticias Financieras EnglishAugust 7, 2020 FridayCopyright 2020 Content Engine, LLC.All Rights ReservedCopyright 2020 CE Noticias Financieras All Rights ReservedLength: 369 wordsBodyU.S. President Donald Trumpsigned an executive order as a "national emergency" to block the country's transactions with Bytedance, the Tik Tok app's parent company dated September 20.The order is also directed towards Tencent,the Chinese multinational in charge of brands such as Riot Games, Epic Games, Miniclip, TiMi Studios and the wechat courier service."The expansion in the United States of mobile applications developed and owned by companies in China continues to threaten the national security, foreign policy, and economy of the United States. At this time, action must be taken to address the threat posed by a particular mobile application: Tik Tok," the executive order said.For the time being, the Department of Homeland Security; The Transportation Security Administration; and the US Armed Forces have banned the use of the app on government phones. Security issues in Tik TokAccording to the US government, the app automatically captures a lot of information from its users; including data such as location and search and browsing history. In that regard, the Trump administration assured that information collection threatens to allow the Chinese government access to personal information and property of American citizens."Potentially, it would allow China to locate the locations of federal employees and contractors, build reports of personal information to blackmail and lead to corporate espionage," he added.Tik Tok defends himselfIn previous days, Vanessa Pappas,the U.S. director general of the app, appreciated the support of millions of Americans who use Tik Tok on a daily basis and noted that they have no plans to go anywhere."Tik Tok is a home for creators and artists to express themselves and their ideas and connect with people with different backgrounds. We are proud of all the diverse communities that call Tik Tok their home. I'm also proud of our 1,500 American employees who work in the app every day; and the 10,000 additional jobs we're going to bring to the country in the next three years," he added.In addition, he said that they are working on creating a totally secure app, because it is the right thing to do. However, he gave no further clarification on this issue.Load-Date: August 8, 2020End of Document

Trump announces he will ban TikTok use in U.S.CE Noticias Financieras EnglishAugust 1, 2020 SaturdayCopyright 2020 Content Engine, LLC.All Rights ReservedCopyright 2020 CE Noticias Financieras All Rights ReservedLength: 589 wordsBodyUS President Donald Trump announced Friday that he will ban the Chinese-owned social network TikTok in the United States, faced with concerns that the platform might be used by Beijing to spy. The announcement is a new step in the Republican Administration's escalation of hostilities towards the Chinese technology sector."As far as TikTok is concerned, we're going to ban it in the United States," Trump said in statements to reporters on the presidential Air Force One plane. The president added that he could take action this Saturday by resorting to emergency economic power or through an executive order, a mechanism that would allow him to exclude threats on the Network to U.S. national security.TikTok is a very popular video application among young people, whose parent company is ByteDance, based in China, and has around 1 billion users worldwide. The app has been downloaded 165 million times in the United States. The Wall Street Journal and the Bloomberg agency anticipated that Trump was planning to announce a decision ordering ByteDance to sell his operation in the United States, estimating that the service could be used by Chinese secret services. ByteDance would be willing to sell his shares in the U.S. in reaction to Trump's veto, a source related to the process has told The New York Times on Saturday.Sources cited by The Washington Post say Microsoft is negotiating to buy it, for a price that could reach several tens of billions of dollars. Microsoft's acquisition of production would suddenly place the U.S. company at the forefront of technology, and substantially change the map of social media in the United States. E later this week, in his testimony in Congress with the bosses of Google, Apple and Amazon, an audience in which Microsoft, Facebook founder Mark Zuckerberg, was not present, he referred to TikTok as his rival. On Friday, on Air Force One, the president made it clear that he is not in favor of an agreement that allows an American company to purchase TikTok's operation in the U.S.Members of the Administration and congressmen have expressed concern that the Chinese government has access to personal data of millions of U.S. citizens, that the social network will be used by Beijing for espionage purposes. The secretary of state himself, Mike Pompeo, said earlier this month that the United States was "certainly" "contemplating" banning TikTok. The Pentagon already recommended in December that members of the Army not use the application.TikTok has denied any ties to the Beijing Government. The company has promised this week a high level of transparency, being open to allowing even revisions of its algorithms. "We are not politicians, we do not accept political publicity and we do not have a political agenda; our only goal is to remain a dynamic platform for everyone to enjoy. TikTok has become the ultimate target, but we're not the enemy," the social network's top official, Kevin Mayer, said in a post this week. The company's spokesman Hilary McQuaide declined to comment on Trump's announcement but expressed her "confidence in TikTok's long-term success."Last June, TikTok made headlines after hundreds of social media users, as well as teens fond of the K-pop music genre, were credited with sabotaging a President Trump rally in Tulsa, Oklahoma, mobilizing their users to register as attendees of the event to makebelieve to the organizers that the attendance was going to be much greater. The rally had a much more modest call than the president's campaign expected.Load-Date: August 2, 2020End of Document| About LexisNexis | Privacy Policy | Terms & Conditions | Copyright
